### 80
This is affine in \(T\): \(T(c0+c1\epsilon+c2\log(c3\epsilon+1)) + (c4+c5\epsilon+c6\log(c3\epsilon+1))\).
GT expanded is also affine in \(T\), so check if coefficients can match:
- Candidate’s coefficient of \(T\) is \(c0 + c1\epsilon + c2\log(c3\epsilon+1)\): **no \(\epsilon\log(\epsilon+1)\)** term.
- GT’s coefficient of \(T\) (collecting \(T\) terms) includes a term proportional to \(\epsilon\) and a term proportional to \(\log(\epsilon+1)\), but **also** the \(\epsilon\) coefficient is a constant (ok) and the \(\log\) coefficient is constant (ok). However GT also has a constant-in-\(\epsilon\) contribution to the \(T\) coefficient (from \(-0.478482(T-352.18)\)), which candidate can represent via \(c0\).
So far seems plausible. But the **intercept** (non-\(T\) part) in GT is not just \(a + b\epsilon + d\log(\epsilon+1)\); it also contains the shift \(352.1818\) coupled consistently across all three \((T-352.18)\) pieces, which enforces specific relationships between the \(T\)-coefficient and the constant term. Candidate 80 has independent constants \(c4,c5,c6\) and does not enforce the same shift structure—but that’s fine because we only need equality, not same decomposition.
Critical mismatch: GT has a **\(T\epsilon\)** term with coefficient \(-96.8294*0.00975241\) (nonzero). Candidate 80 has \(T*c1*\epsilon\), so can match that. GT has \(T\log(\epsilon+1)\) term with coefficient \(8.06201\), candidate has \(T*c2\log(c3\epsilon+1)\), so set \(c3=1\), \(c2=8.06201\). Good.
Now check GT also has a **\(T\epsilon\)** term plus a **\(\epsilon\)** term and a **\(\epsilon T\)** term derived from the same original; candidate can fit those independently via \(c1\) (for \(T\epsilon\)) and \(c5\) (for \(\epsilon\)). Likewise for \(\log\) via \(c2\) and \(c6\), and constant via \(c0\) and \(c4\).
So candidate 80 actually *can* represent any function of the form:
\[
T(A_0 + A_1\epsilon + A_2\log(\epsilon+1)) + (B_0 + B_1\epsilon + B_2\log(\epsilon+1)).
\]
GT, when expanded, is exactly of that form (affine in \(T\), with only \(\epsilon\) and \(\log(\epsilon+1)\) dependence, no products like \(\epsilon\log(\epsilon+1)\)). Therefore candidate 80 **can match** by choosing constants appropriately (set \(c3=1\) and solve linear coefficients).
=> Candidate 80 matches.
